Orientation and final conventions
- Axes: x east (+), y north (+), z up (+). Bridge long axis along y, width along x, depth along z.

# builder (gpt-5) (ThoughtEvent): 

Introduction to available build tools and how we will use them step by step

- functions.start
  - What it does: Creates the initial starting block (the “Base”) and places it at a specified position and rotation.
  - What I need: init_shift [x, y, z], init_rotation [yaw, pitch, roll] in degrees, and a descriptive note. For this bridge, we’ll create the default 1×1×1 Stone base at the origin (0,0,0). The note is very important to identify the Base’s role (e.g., “Central deck base at (0,0,0)”).

- functions.attach_block_to
  - What it does: Attaches a new block to a specific face of an existing block. Available new_block types: Small Wooden Block, Powered Wheel, Torch, Water Cannon. We will only use Small Wooden Block per your blueprint (no powered components).
  - What I need: base_block ID, face (e.g., North/South/East/West/Top/Bottom), new_block type, and a descriptive note. The note argument is critical to mark the block’s function and position (e.g., “Deck center row y=+1, x=0”).

- functions.connect_blocks
  - What it does: Connects two existing blocks via a connector. Available connector types: Brace, Winch. We will use Brace for structural diagonals (no motion).
  - What I need: block_a ID and its face, block_b ID and its face, connector type, and a descriptive note indicating the bay, direction, and function (very important identifier). Faces must be reasonably separated; I will verify faces with get_block_details if needed.

- functions.remove_block
  - What it does: Removes a block by ID if we need to correct something.
  - What I need: block_id. The note is not applicable here, but I’ll document context in chat.

- functions.reset
  - What it does: Clears the entire machine to an empty state.
  - What I need: No arguments. I will only use if you instruct or if a full rebuild is required.

- functions.flip_spin
  - What it does: Flips spin direction of a spinning block. Not relevant here since we won’t use powered/spinning parts.

- functions.shift_block
  - What it does: Adjusts a block’s position slightly after attachment (offset range each axis: −0.5..+0.5). Useful if an attachment overlaps or needs fine alignment.
  - What I need: block_id and shift_real [dx, dy, dz]. I will explain and annotate with context when used.

- functions.twist_block
  - What it does: Rotates a block around its rooted surface by an angle (degrees). Helpful for orienting pointer-like elements; typically not needed for cubic wooden blocks, but can align braces if necessary.
  - What I need: block_id and angle, plus context in note here in the chat.

- functions.get_block_details
  - What it does: Returns a specific block’s position, rotation, and face details. I’ll use this to confirm face names and geometry when needed (especially for connections).
  - What I need: block_id.

- functions.get_machine_summary
  - What it does: Returns an overall machine state (no face captions). It is mandatory to use this tool for a final check before finishing. I will remind you and run it before we conclude.

Plan to execute your blueprint
- I will build one block at a time and make one tool call per message.
- Start by placing the Base at (0,0,0).
- Then proceed with the deck center row (IDs 1–21), left row (22–43), right row (44–65), vertical posts (66–89), bottom chords (90–127), bottom transverse ties (128–133), and finally the diagonal braces (134–143) using connector “Brace”.
- For each block/brace, I will use a precise note to match your identifiers and functions.
- I will not infer or change any part beyond your instructions.

Proceeding to create the Base now.
